# FINDINGS
# ─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────

findings:

  - id: FC-01
    severity: HIGH
    category: citation_wrong
    location: >
      §"Source overview" — the claim at line 52 that Forsyth 1987's work offers "treatment
      of East Asian combat-myth" that "supplies the wider scholarly context within which the
      comparative chaoskampf reading of the Susanoo / Orochi narrative has been advanced."
      EVIDENCE tag at line 53: source_id=forsyth-1987 ; loc=on East Asian combat-myth.
      Also affects the two subsequent Forsyth EVIDENCE tags (lines 190, 193) in
      §"The chaoskampf label as applied from outside," where Forsyth is cited for the
      comparativist reading of the Susanoo/Orochi episode. This is the same Forsyth scope
      misuse flagged HIGH in Ch20 (Slavic-Baltic factcheck) and Ch21 (Gonggong factcheck).
    claim_text: >
      "The chapter's general comparative anchor for the long-arc combat-myth tradition is
      Neil Forsyth's The Old Enemy: Satan and the Combat Myth, published by Princeton
      University Press in 1987, whose treatment of East Asian combat-myth supplies the wider
      scholarly context within which the comparative chaoskampf reading of the Susanoo /
      Orochi narrative has been advanced and against which the chapter's area-specialist
      counter-framing is set." (line 52)
    problem: >
      Forsyth 1987 (The Old Enemy: Satan and the Combat Myth) is a study of the combat myth
      tradition from ancient Mesopotamia (Sumer) through Ugaritic, Biblical Hebrew,
      intertestamental Jewish, and New Testament / early Christian apocalyptic literature.
      Per sources.yaml: "Traces the combat myth from Sumer through Judeo-Christian
      apocalyptic." The book does NOT treat East Asian combat-myth traditions — Japanese
      mythology is entirely outside Forsyth's scope. The claim that Forsyth's "treatment of
      East Asian combat-myth supplies the wider scholarly context" is therefore factually
      incorrect. The loc "on East Asian combat-myth" in the EVIDENCE tag is unsupported.
      The severity is HIGH for the line 52 / line 53 claim because it asserts Forsyth as a
      content-source for East Asian combat-myth scholarship, which the book's documented
      scope does not support.
      The two subsequent Forsyth citations (lines 189-193) are less severe: they use Forsyth
      more defensibly as a representative of the wider comparativist combat-myth tradition
      (which Forsyth does cover for the Western trajectory) and frame the Susanoo episode as
      an episode that "has been read" within that tradition — a weaker attribution. However,
      these too carry the same source_id=forsyth-1987 ; loc=on East Asian combat-myth EVIDENCE
      tag, which mislabels the location as "East Asian combat-myth" content that Forsyth does
      not provide. Those two EVIDENCE locs should be corrected to "on the comparativist combat-
      myth tradition (Near Eastern — Western trajectory)" even if the wider contextual use of
      Forsyth is maintained.
      This finding is a recurrence of the Forsyth misuse pattern identified in:
      - Ch20 factcheck FC-01 (Forsyth as anchor for Slavic-Baltic material)
      - Ch21 factcheck FC-01 (Forsyth as anchor for Chinese combat-myth)
      The brief for Ch23 specifies Forsyth only as sources.secondary with loc "on East Asian
      combat-myth" — the brief itself propagates the incorrect loc, which must be corrected
      at the brief level to prevent the error recurring in the chapter draft.
    evidence: >
      sources.yaml forsyth-1987 notes: "Traces the combat myth from Sumer through Judeo-
      Christian apocalyptic. Full catalog-level treatment." The Sumer-to-Christian-apocalyptic
      trajectory does not include East Asian (Japanese) mythology. Trained knowledge of
      Forsyth 1987 confirms the book's chapters treat: Mesopotamian (Enuma Elish, Chaoskampf),
      Ugaritic (Baal / Yam / Mot / Lotan), Biblical (Rahab, Leviathan, Daniel), intertesta-
      mental (1 Enoch, Jubilees), and New Testament / Revelation material. No chapter on East
      Asian myth. Ch20 factcheck FC-01 and Ch21 factcheck FC-01 identified the same pattern.
    recommended_fix: >
      (1) Line 52: Replace "whose treatment of East Asian combat-myth supplies the wider
      scholarly context" with "whose treatment of the long-arc Near Eastern and Western
      combat-myth tradition supplies the wider comparativist scholarly context." The sentence
      should make clear that Forsyth covers the Western/Near Eastern trajectory and that the
      Susanoo episode is brought into comparison with that tradition by the comparativist
      move, not that Forsyth himself covers East Asian myth.
      (2) EVIDENCE tag at line 53: Replace loc="on East Asian combat-myth" with
      loc="on the Near Eastern and Western combat-myth comparative tradition."
      (3) EVIDENCE tags at lines 190 and 193: Same loc correction — replace "on East Asian
      combat-myth" with "on the comparativist combat-myth tradition (Near Eastern–Western
      trajectory)." The body claims at lines 189 and 192 themselves are more defensible and
      may not require body-prose changes, but the loc is wrong in all three EVIDENCE tags.
      (4) Brief correction: Update sources.secondary entry for forsyth-1987 in brief
      23-susanoo-orochi.yaml: change loc from "on East Asian combat-myth" to "on the
      comparativist combat-myth tradition (Near Eastern–Western trajectory)."
      At human review, check whether a Japan-specialist secondary source (e.g., Matsumura
      1954 or a current English-language survey of Japanese mythology scholarship) should be
      added to sources.yaml to provide genuinely East-Asian-specialist grounding for the
      claim that the comparativist chaoskampf reading of Susanoo/Orochi "has been advanced"
      within the scholarly tradition.

  - id: FC-02
    severity: MEDIUM
    category: unverified
    location: >
      §"The metallurgical-allegory reading" — the claim at line 170 that the metallurgical-
      allegory reading is "developed in detail by Nelly Naumann and taken up by subsequent
      specialists including Jun'ichi Isomae, Michael Como, and Herman Ooms." Three of the four
      named scholars (Isomae, Como, Ooms) are not in sources.yaml. The writer's INFERENCE
      marker at line 176 explicitly flags this as a risk requiring factcheck resolution.
    claim_text: >
      "The principal area-specialist reading of the Yamata no Orochi episode in current
      scholarship — developed in detail by Nelly Naumann and taken up by subsequent specialists
      including Jun'ichi Isomae, Michael Como, and Herman Ooms — is metallurgical-allegorical."
      (line 170)
    problem: >
      Three of the four area-specialists named as holding the metallurgical-allegory reading
      (Isomae, Como, Ooms) are not in sources.yaml and were not verifiable at this audit stage.
      The writer correctly flags this in the INFERENCE marker (line 176), noting that "Isomae,
      Como, and Ooms are NAMED in the body prose per the brief's area-specialist citation policy
      and per scope.md §'Appropriation protocol' requirement of two area-specialists by name in
      the first factual pass, but their works are not in the current sources.yaml registry."
      The claim that all four scholars share the metallurgical-allegory reading is plausible
      given that Naumann is the foundational source and the names appear in the brief's
      special_instructions — suggesting the brief-author had access to scholarship identifying
      these scholars as holding this reading. However, the specific attribution cannot be
      verified from the current sources base. If any of the three additional scholars do NOT
      hold the metallurgical-allegory reading in the form stated, the body claim's attribution
      is overstated.
      Assessed MEDIUM (not HIGH) because: (a) Naumann 1996 is the foundational and documented
      source for the metallurgical-allegory reading and is sufficient to sustain the body claims
      about the reading itself; (b) the three additional scholars are named "including" (not
      "exclusively"), so the attribution is to a list of follow-on scholars rather than to any
      one of them specifically; (c) the writer explicitly flags the risk in the INFERENCE marker,
      so this is a known-and-flagged gap rather than a silent bridge.
    evidence: >
      sources.yaml: isomae (Jun'ichi Isomae), como (Michael Como), and ooms (Herman Ooms)
      do not appear as entries. The brief 23-susanoo-orochi.yaml special_instructions names
      all four scholars as the area-specialists whose framing is load-bearing, but does not
      cite specific publication details for Isomae, Como, or Ooms. The writer's INFERENCE
      marker at line 176 explicitly acknowledges the risk. The Ch23 writer completion record
      (11-chapter-claims-ch23.done.yaml) flags these as missing from sources.yaml — per the
      instruction not to consult that file before forming findings, this is independently
      confirmed by this audit's sources.yaml check.
    recommended_fix: >
      At human review: (1) Verify that Isomae 2010 (likely Jun'ichi Isomae, Myth, Protest,
      and Struggle in Japanese Literature, or a related monograph on Japanese mythology),
      Como 2009 (likely Michael Como, Weaving and Binding: Immigrant Gods and Female
      Immortals in Ancient Japan, or another Como monograph on early Japanese religion), and
      Ooms 2009 (likely Herman Ooms, Imperial Politics and Symbolics in Ancient Japan: The
      Tenmu Dynasty, 650-800, or a related work) each develop or endorse the metallurgical-
      allegory reading of the Yamata no Orochi episode. (2) If confirmed, add all three to
      sources.yaml and update the EVIDENCE tag for the line 170 claim to cite one or more
      of them alongside Naumann. (3) If any of the three does not specifically endorse the
      metallurgical-allegory reading, downgrade the body claim at line 170 to "developed in
      detail by Nelly Naumann, with subsequent area-specialist attention by [those who do]."
      This is MEDIUM rather than HIGH because the narrative claims in the claims document are
      all anchored to Naumann 1996 alone via their EVIDENCE tags; the three additional scholars
      appear only in body-prose attribution, not in EVIDENCE tokens. No individual claim depends
      on Isomae, Como, or Ooms specifically in an EVIDENCE token.

  - id: FC-03
    severity: LOW
    category: unverified
    location: >
      §"Source overview" — the publisher attribution for Philippi 1968 at lines 31 and 46,
      and the ISBN / publisher pairing in sources.yaml vs. the claims document. Line 31
      writes "Princeton/Tokyo: University of Tokyo Press; ISBN 9780691611358"; line 46 writes
      "Tokyo: University of Tokyo Press, 1968; ISBN 9780691611358"; sources.yaml full_citation
      writes "Tokyo: University of Tokyo Press, 1968" with ISBN 9780691611358.
    claim_text: >
      "Philippi 1968, Kojiki (Princeton/Tokyo: University of Tokyo Press; ISBN 9780691611358)"
      — line 31; "Philippi 1968, Kojiki (Tokyo: University of Tokyo Press, 1968; ISBN
      9780691611358)" — line 46.
    problem: >
      The ISBN 9780691611358 carries the prefix 0-691, which is the Princeton University Press
      ISBN prefix. The original 1968 University of Tokyo Press edition of Philippi's Kojiki
      was co-published with Princeton University Press; later Princeton paperback reprints
      carry the 0-691-prefixed ISBN. The claims document's combination of "University of Tokyo
      Press" as publisher with a Princeton University Press-prefixed ISBN creates a bibliographic
      inconsistency. The two in-text citations are also inconsistent with each other (line 31:
      "Princeton/Tokyo: University of Tokyo Press"; line 46: "Tokyo: University of Tokyo Press,
      1968"). The content of the translation is the same regardless of which edition or reprint
      is cited; this is a LOW bibliographic inconsistency, not a factual error about what the
      text says.
    evidence: >
      ISBN prefix 978-0-691 = Princeton University Press. The sources.yaml full_citation
      reads "Tokyo: University of Tokyo Press, 1968" with identifier_value "9780691611358".
      The two in-text footnotes at lines 31 and 46 are inconsistent with each other. This
      inconsistency is already present at the sources.yaml level and propagates into the
      claims document.
    recommended_fix: >
      Standardise the Philippi Kojiki citation across sources.yaml and the claims document.
      The most accurate description is that the work was originally published jointly by
      the University of Tokyo Press and Princeton University Press in 1968. The ISBN
      9780691611358 is the Princeton paperback reprint ISBN. The citation should either:
      (a) Use "University of Tokyo Press / Princeton University Press, 1968" consistently
      with the Princeton-prefix ISBN; or (b) find the original 1968 UTokyo edition ISBN and
      use that. Option (a) is the simpler fix. Update sources.yaml full_citation accordingly,
      and align the two in-text footnotes to a single consistent form. This is LOW because
      the work is unambiguously identified and the content is identical across editions.

  - id: FC-04
    severity: NOTE
    category: unverified
    location: >
      §"The chaoskampf label as applied from outside" — the APPROPRIATION-FLAG marker
      (scope.md §"Appropriation protocol" point 2) is absent from the claims document.
      The claims document does contain an extensive outside-framing apparatus, but does not
      include an explicit [APPROPRIATION-FLAG:] marker as specified in scope.md.
    claim_text: >
      scope.md §"Appropriation protocol" point 2: "Record any specialist objection to the
      chaoskampf framing in an [APPROPRIATION-FLAG:] marker, which the comparative chapter
      must address rather than paper over."
    problem: >
      The chapter's entire framing is an appropriation-protocol compliance exercise, and the
      VARIANT marker at line 198 explicitly encodes the area-specialist vs. comparativist
      reading choice. However, the specific [APPROPRIATION-FLAG:] marker called for by
      scope.md §"Appropriation protocol" point 2 does not appear anywhere in the document.
      The VARIANT marker performs a similar function, and the INFERENCE marker at line 176
      discusses the appropriation risk; but neither of these is the [APPROPRIATION-FLAG:]
      marker. The scope.md requirement is for a specifically named marker type.
      This is flagged NOTE rather than MEDIUM because: (a) the chapter's overall framing
      apparatus (INFERENCE + VARIANT together) functionally covers the appropriation-flag
      requirement; (b) the scope.md description of the flag is brief and does not specify
      whether it is required in addition to or instead of other markers; (c) the comparative
      chapter that is to "address rather than paper over" the objection (Part II C8, ch. 41)
      is identified and referenced in the VARIANT marker reason field. The absence is a
      marker-discipline note, not a substantive framing failure.
    evidence: >
      scope.md §"Appropriation protocol" point 2: explicit [APPROPRIATION-FLAG:] marker
      required when area specialists object to the chaoskampf framing. The document contains
      INFERENCE and VARIANT markers but no [APPROPRIATION-FLAG:] marker. Search confirms
      zero occurrences of "APPROPRIATION-FLAG" in the claims document.
    recommended_fix: >
      Add an [APPROPRIATION-FLAG:] marker in §"The chaoskampf label as applied from outside"
      immediately before or after the VARIANT marker at line 198. The marker should:
      (1) identify the objecting specialists (Naumann, Isomae, Como, Ooms);
      (2) state the objection precisely (the episode's load-bearing function is sword-etiology
      and metallurgical-allegorical-political charter, not cosmogonic combat);
      (3) note that Part II C8 (ch. 41) is the locus for addressing this objection in the
      comparative analysis. The chapter draft can re-use the wording of the existing VARIANT
      marker's primary field and reason field almost verbatim for this purpose.
